<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colonial_empires_in_1800.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1425" decoding="async" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Colonial_empires_in_1800.svg/300px-Colonial_empires_in_1800.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Colonial_empires_in_1800.svg/450px-Colonial_empires_in_1800.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Colonial_empires_in_1800.svg/600px-Colonial_empires_in_1800.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colonial_empires_in_1800.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The cumulative crises and disruptions of Napoleon's <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">invasion of Spain</a> led to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">independence</a> of most of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spain's American colonies</a> (yellow) and the <a href="/wiki/Independence_of_Brazil" title="Independence of Brazil">independence of Brazil</a> (green).</div></div></div>
<p>Most of the new nations were abolished and returned to prewar owners in 1814. However, Artz emphasizes the benefits the Italians gained from the French Revolution:
</p>
<dl><dd>For nearly two decades the Italians had excellent codes of law, a fair system of taxation, a better economic situation, and more religious and intellectual toleration than they had known for centuries.... Everywhere old physical, economic, and intellectual barriers had been thrown down and the Italians had begun to be aware of a common nationality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Likewise in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Switzerland" title="History of Switzerland">Switzerland</a> the long-term impact of the French Revolution has been assessed by Martin:
</p>
<dl><dd>It proclaimed the equality of citizens before the law, equality of languages, freedom of thought and faith; it created a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_citizenship" title="Swiss citizenship">Swiss citizenship</a>, basis of our modern nationality, and the separation of powers, of which the old regime had no conception; it suppressed internal tariffs and other economic restraints; it unified weights and measures, reformed civil and penal law, authorized mixed marriages (between Catholics and Protestants), suppressed torture and improved justice; it developed education and public works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>The greatest impact came of course in France itself. In addition to effects similar to those in Italy and Switzerland, France saw the introduction of the principle of legal equality, and the downgrading of the once powerful and rich <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_France" title="Catholic Church in France">Catholic Church</a> to just a bureau controlled by the government. Power became centralized in Paris, with its strong bureaucracy and an army supplied by conscripting all young men. French politics were permanently polarized – new names were given, "left" and "right" for the supporters and opponents of the principles of the Revolution.
</p><p>British historian <a href="/wiki/Max_Hastings" title="Max Hastings">Max Hastings</a> says there is no question that as a military genius Napoleon ranks with <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> and <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a> in greatness. However, in the political realm, historians debate whether Napoleon was "an enlightened despot who laid the foundations of modern Europe or, instead, a megalomaniac who wrought greater misery than any man before the coming of Hitler".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_the_19th_century" title="Christianity in the 19th century">Christianity in the 19th century</a></div>
<p>By the 19th century, governments increasingly took over traditional religious roles, paying much more attention to efficiency and uniformity than to religiosity. Secular bodies took control of education away from the churches, abolished taxes and tithes for the support of <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">established religions</a>, and excluded bishops from the upper houses. Secular laws increasingly regulated marriage and divorce, and maintaining birth and death registers became the duty of local officials. Although the numerous <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_United_States" title="Religion in the United States">religious denominations in the United States</a> founded many colleges and universities, that was almost exclusively a state function across Europe.  Imperial powers protected <a href="/wiki/Christian_mission" title="Christian mission">Christian missionaries</a> in African and Asian colonies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> In France and other largely Catholic nations, <a href="/wiki/Anti-clericalism" title="Anti-clericalism">anti-clerical</a> political movements tried to reduce the role of the Catholic Church. Likewise briefly in Germany in the 1870s there was a fierce <a href="/wiki/Kulturkampf" title="Kulturkampf">Kulturkampf</a> (culture war) against <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Germany" title="Catholic Church in Germany">Catholics</a>, but the Catholics successfully fought back. The Catholic Church concentrated more power in the papacy and fought against <a href="/wiki/Secularism" title="Secularism">secularism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialism</a>. It sponsored devotional reforms that gained wide support among the churchgoers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Protestantism">Protestantism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Protestantism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Historian <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Scott_Latourette" title="Kenneth Scott Latourette">Kenneth Scott Latourette</a> argues that the outlook for Protestantism at the start of the 19th century was discouraging. It was a regional religion based in <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_Europe" title="Northwestern Europe">Northwestern Europe</a>, with an outpost in the sparsely settled United States. It was closely allied with government, as in Scandinavia, the Netherlands, Prussia, and especially Great Britain. The alliance came at the expense of independence, as the government made the basic policy decisions, down to such details as the salaries of ministers and location of new churches. The dominant intellectual currents of the Enlightenment promoted rationalism, and most Protestant leaders preached a sort of deism. Intellectually, the new methods of historical and anthropological study undermine automatic acceptance of biblical stories, as did the sciences of geology and biology. Industrialization was a strongly negative factor, as workers who moved to the city seldom joined churches. The gap between the church and the unchurched grew rapidly, and secular forces, based both in socialism and liberalism undermine the prestige of religion. Despite the negative forces, Protestantism demonstrated a striking vitality by 1900. Shrugging off Enlightenment rationalism, Protestants embraced <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">romanticism</a>, with the stress on the personal and the invisible. Entirely fresh ideas as expressed by <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Schleiermacher" title="Friedrich Schleiermacher">Friedrich Schleiermacher</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soren_Kierkegaard" title="Soren Kierkegaard">Soren Kierkegaard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_Ritschl" title="Albrecht Ritschl">Albrecht Ritschl</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adolf_von_Harnack" title="Adolf von Harnack">Adolf von Harnack</a> restored the intellectual power of theology. There was more attention to historic creeds such as the Augsburg, the Heidelberg, and the Westminster confessions. In England, <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicans</a> emphasize the historically Catholic components of their heritage, as the <a href="/wiki/High_church" title="High church">High Church</a> element reintroduced vestments and incense into their rituals. The stirrings of <a href="/wiki/Pietism" title="Pietism">pietism</a> on the Continent, and <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">evangelicalism</a> in Britain expanded enormously, leading the devout away from an emphasis on formality and ritual and toward an inner sensibility toward personal relationship to Christ. Social activities, in education and in opposition to social vices such as slavery, alcoholism and poverty provided new opportunities for social service. Above all, worldwide missionary activity became a highly prized goal, proving quite successful in close cooperation with European colonialists, particularly during the <a href="/wiki/New_Imperialism" title="New Imperialism">New Imperialism</a> period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nations_rising">Nations rising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Nations rising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_relations_of_the_Great_Powers_(1814%E2%80%931919)" title="International relations of the Great Powers (1814–1919)">International relations of the Great Powers (1814–1919)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Revolution" title="Serbian Revolution">Serbian Revolution</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">Italian unification</a>, <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">Revolutions of 1848</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence" title="Greek War of Independence">Greek War of Independence</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ereignisblatt_aus_den_revolution%C3%A4ren_M%C3%A4rztagen_18.-19._M%C3%A4rz_1848_mit_einer_Barrikadenszene_aus_der_Breiten_Strasse,_Berlin_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="705" data-file-width="899" decoding="async" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ereignisblatt_aus_den_revolution%C3%A4ren_M%C3%A4rztagen_18.-19._M%C3%A4rz_1848_mit_einer_Barrikadenszene_aus_der_Breiten_Strasse%2C_Berlin_01.jpg/220px-Ereignisblatt_aus_den_revolution%C3%A4ren_M%C3%A4rztagen_18.-19._M%C3%A4rz_1848_mit_einer_Barrikadenszene_aus_der_Breiten_Strasse%2C_Berlin_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ereignisblatt_aus_den_revolution%C3%A4ren_M%C3%A4rztagen_18.-19._M%C3%A4rz_1848_mit_einer_Barrikadenszene_aus_der_Breiten_Strasse%2C_Berlin_01.jpg/330px-Ereignisblatt_aus_den_revolution%C3%A4ren_M%C3%A4rztagen_18.-19._M%C3%A4rz_1848_mit_einer_Barrikadenszene_aus_der_Breiten_Strasse%2C_Berlin_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Ereignisblatt_aus_den_revolution%C3%A4ren_M%C3%A4rztagen_18.-19._M%C3%A4rz_1848_mit_einer_Barrikadenszene_aus_der_Breiten_Strasse%2C_Berlin_01.jpg/440px-Ereignisblatt_aus_den_revolution%C3%A4ren_M%C3%A4rztagen_18.-19._M%C3%A4rz_1848_mit_einer_Barrikadenszene_aus_der_Breiten_Strasse%2C_Berlin_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ereignisblatt_aus_den_revolution%C3%A4ren_M%C3%A4rztagen_18.-19._M%C3%A4rz_1848_mit_einer_Barrikadenszene_aus_der_Breiten_Strasse,_Berlin_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cheering the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">Revolutions of 1848</a> in Berlin</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Emerging_nationalism">Emerging nationalism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Emerging nationalism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Rise_of_nationalism_in_Europe" title="Rise of nationalism in Europe">Rise of nationalism in Europe</a></div>
<p>The political development of nationalism and the push for <a href="/wiki/Popular_sovereignty" title="Popular sovereignty">popular sovereignty</a> culminated with the ethnic/national revolutions of Europe. During the 19th century nationalism became one of the most significant political and social forces in history; it is typically listed among the top causes of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>Napoleon's conquests of the German and Italian states around 1800–1806 played a major role in stimulating nationalism and the demands for national unity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Germany">Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Germany" title="Unification of Germany">Unification of Germany</a></div>
<p>In the German states east of Prussia Napoleon abolished many of the old or medieval relics, such as <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Dissolution of the Holy Roman Empire">dissolving the Holy Roman Empire</a> in 1806.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> He imposed rational legal systems and demonstrated how dramatic changes were possible. For example, his organization of the <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_the_Rhine" title="Confederation of the Rhine">Confederation of the Rhine</a> in 1806 promoted a feeling of <a href="/wiki/German_nationalism" title="German nationalism">German nationalism</a>. Nationalists sought to encompass masculinity in their quest for strength and unity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> In the 1860s it was Prussian chancellor <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck" title="Otto von Bismarck">Otto von Bismarck</a> who achieved German unification in 1870 after the many smaller states followed Prussia's leadership in wars against Denmark, Austria and France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Italy">Italy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Italy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Italy" title="Unification of Italy">Unification of Italy</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Italian_nationalism" title="Italian nationalism">Italian nationalism</a> emerged in the 19th century and was the driving force for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">Italian unification</a> or the "Risorgimento" (meaning the Resurgence or revival). It was the political and intellectual movement that consolidated different states of the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Peninsula" title="Italian Peninsula">Italian Peninsula</a> into the single state of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a> in 1860. The memory of the Risorgimento is central to both Italian nationalism and Italian historiography.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Missolonghi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="772" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Missolonghi.jpg/220px-Missolonghi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Missolonghi.jpg/330px-Missolonghi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Missolonghi.jpg/440px-Missolonghi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Missolonghi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Beginning in 1821, the <a href="/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence" title="Greek War of Independence">Greek War of Independence</a> began as a rebellion by Greek revolutionaries against the ruling Ottoman Empire.</div></div></div>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia">Serbia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Serbia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Serbia" title="History of Serbia">History of Serbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Austria-Hungary" title="Dissolution of Austria-Hungary">Dissolution of Austria-Hungary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Creation_of_Yugoslavia" title="Creation of Yugoslavia">Creation of Yugoslavia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Breakup_of_Yugoslavia-TRY2.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1242" data-file-width="1545" decoding="async" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia-TRY2.gif/250px-Breakup_of_Yugoslavia-TRY2.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia-TRY2.gif/375px-Breakup_of_Yugoslavia-TRY2.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Breakup_of_Yugoslavia-TRY2.gif/500px-Breakup_of_Yugoslavia-TRY2.gif 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Breakup_of_Yugoslavia-TRY2.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Breakup of Yugoslavia</div></div></div>
<p>For centuries the <a href="/wiki/Serbian_Orthodox_Church" title="Serbian Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christian</a> <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Serbs" title="Ottoman Serbs">Serbs</a> were ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Islam in the Ottoman Empire">Muslim</a>-controlled <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>. The success of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_revolution" title="Serbian revolution">Serbian revolution</a> (1804–1817) against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Ottoman_Serbia" title="History of Ottoman Serbia">Ottoman rule</a> in 1817 marked the foundation of modern <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia" title="Principality of Serbia">Principality of Serbia</a>. It achieved <i>de facto</i> independence in 1867 and finally gained recognition by the Great Powers in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berlin_Congress" title="Berlin Congress">Berlin Congress</a> of 1878. The Serbs developed a larger vision for nationalism in <a href="/wiki/Pan-Slavism" title="Pan-Slavism">Pan-Slavism</a> and with Russian support sought to pull the other Slavs out of the <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austro-Hungarian Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> Austria, with German backing, tried to crush Serbia in 1914 but Russia intervened, thus igniting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a> in which Austria dissolved into nation states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1918, the region of <a href="/wiki/Vojvodina" title="Vojvodina">Vojvodina</a> proclaimed its <a href="/wiki/Banat,_Ba%C4%8Dka_and_Baranja" title="Banat, Bačka and Baranja">secession</a> from Austria-Hungary to unite with the pan-Slavic <a href="/wiki/State_of_Slovenes,_Croats_and_Serbs" title="State of Slovenes, Croats and Serbs">State of Slovenes, Croats and Serbs</a>; the Kingdom of Serbia joined the union on 1 December 1918, and the country was named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Serbs,_Croats,_and_Slovenes" title="Kingdom of Serbs, Croats, and Slovenes">Kingdom of Serbs, Croats, and Slovenes</a>. It was renamed <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, which was never able to tame the multiple nationalities and religions and it flew apart in <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">civil war</a> in the 1990s.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">Greece</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Greece">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence" title="Greek War of Independence">Greek War of Independence</a></div>
<p>The Greek drive for independence from the Ottoman Empire inspired supporters across Christian Europe, especially in Britain. France, Russia and Britain intervened to make this nationalist dream become reality with the <a href="/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence" title="Greek War of Independence">Greek War of Independence</a> (1821-1829/1830).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Bulgaria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_National_Revival" title="Bulgarian National Revival">Bulgarian National Revival</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_awakening_of_Bulgaria" title="National awakening of Bulgaria">National awakening of Bulgaria</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarian</a> modern <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">nationalism</a> emerged under <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman rule</a> in the late 18th and early 19th century, under the influence of western ideas such as liberalism and nationalism, which trickled into the country after the French revolution, mostly via Greece, although there were stirrings in the 18th century. Russia, as a World <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Power" title="Great Power">Great Power</a> of fellow Orthodox Slavs, could appeal to the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarians</a> in a way that Austria could not. An autonomous <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Exarchate" title="Bulgarian Exarchate">Bulgarian Exarchate</a> was established in 1870/1872 for the diocese of Bulgaria as well as for those, wherein at least two-thirds of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Christians</a> were willing to join it. The <a href="/wiki/April_Uprising_of_1876" title="April Uprising of 1876">April Uprising</a> in 1876 indirectly resulted in the <a href="/wiki/Liberation_of_Bulgaria" title="Liberation of Bulgaria">re-establishment of Bulgaria in 1878</a>.
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Poland">Poland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Poland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poland" title="History of Poland">History of Poland</a></div>
<p>The cause of <a href="/wiki/Polish_nationalism" title="Polish nationalism">Polish nationalism</a> was repeatedly frustrated before 1918. In the 1790s, Germany, Russia and Austria <a href="/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland" title="Partitions of Poland">partitioned Poland</a>. Napoleon set up the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Warsaw" title="Duchy of Warsaw">Duchy of Warsaw</a>, a new Polish state that ignited a spirit of nationalism. Russia took it over in 1815 as <a href="/wiki/Congress_Poland" title="Congress Poland">Congress Poland</a> with the tsar as King of Poland. Large-scale nationalist revolts erupted <a href="/wiki/November_Uprising" title="November Uprising">in 1830</a> and <a href="/wiki/January_Uprising" title="January Uprising">1863–64</a> but were harshly crushed by Russia, which tried to <a href="/wiki/Russification_of_Poles_during_the_Partitions" title="Russification of Poles during the Partitions">Russify</a> the <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Poland" title="Culture of Poland">culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Poland" title="Religion in Poland">religion</a>. The collapse of the Russian Empire in the First World War enabled the major powers to reestablish an independent <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Second Polish Republic</a>, which survived until 1939. Meanwhile, Poles in areas controlled by Germany moved into heavy industry but their religion came under attack by Bismarck in the Kulturkampf of the 1870s. The Poles joined German Catholics in a well-organized new <a href="/wiki/Centre_Party_(Germany)" title="Centre Party (Germany)">Centre Party</a>, and defeated Bismarck politically. He responded by stopping the harassment and cooperating with the Centre Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup>
</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Spain">Spain</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Spain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mapa_pol%C3%ADtico_de_Espa%C3%B1a,_1850.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1322" data-file-width="1800" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Mapa_pol%C3%ADtico_de_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_1850.jpg/220px-Mapa_pol%C3%ADtico_de_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_1850.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Mapa_pol%C3%ADtico_de_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_1850.jpg/330px-Mapa_pol%C3%ADtico_de_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_1850.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Mapa_pol%C3%ADtico_de_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_1850.jpg/440px-Mapa_pol%C3%ADtico_de_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_1850.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mapa_pol%C3%ADtico_de_Espa%C3%B1a,_1850.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>School map of Spain from 1850. It can be seen the State divided into four parts:- The "fully constitutional Spain", that includes Castilia, but also Galician-speaking territories. - The "<b>assimilated Spain</b>": territories from the Crown of Aragon, larguely Catalan-speaking territory- the "Foral Spain", which includes Basque-speaking territories- the "Colonial Spain", with last colonial territories.</div></div></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, rooted in the political position of the <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_de_Guzm%C3%A1n,_Count-Duke_of_Olivares" title="Gaspar de Guzmán, Count-Duke of Olivares">Count-Duke of Olivares</a> and the absolutism of <a href="/wiki/Philip_V_of_Spain" title="Philip V of Spain">Philip V</a>, the assimilation of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">Crown of Aragon</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castilian Crown</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Planta_decrees" title="Nueva Planta decrees">Decrees of Nova planta</a> was the first step in the creation of the Spanish nation state. As in other contemporary European states, political union was the first step in the creation of the Spanish nation-state, in this case not on a uniform <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic</a> basis, but through the imposition of the political and cultural characteristics of the dominant ethnic group, in this case the Castilians, over those of other ethnic groups, who became <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">national minorities</a> to be assimilated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> In fact, since the political unification of 1714, Spanish assimilation policies towards Catalan-speaking territories (<a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">Valencia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">Balearic Islands</a>, part of <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">Aragon</a>) and other national minorities have been a historical constant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Recopilació_d'accions_genocides_con_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-Recopilació_d'accions_genocides_con-141">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-142">[142]</a></sup>  The nationalization process accelerated in the 19th century, in parallel to the origin of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_nationalism" title="Spanish nationalism">Spanish nationalism</a>, the social, political and ideological movement that tried to shape a Spanish national identity based on the Castilian model, in conflict with the other historical nations of the State. These nationalist policies, sometimes very aggressive,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-145">[145]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0222_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0222-146">[146]</a></sup> and still in force,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-147">[147]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-148">[148]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:5_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-:5-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> have been, and still are, the seed of repeated territorial conflicts within the State.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>An important component of nationalism was the study of the nation's heritage, emphasizing the <a href="/wiki/National_language" title="National language">national language</a> and literary culture. This stimulated, and was in turn strongly supported by, the emergence of <a href="/wiki/State_school" title="State school">national educational systems</a> reaching the general population. <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> gave way to the national language, and <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_education" title="Compulsory education">compulsory education</a>, with strong support from modernizers and the media, became standard in Germany and eventually the other West European nations. Voting reforms extended the franchise to the previously excluded elements. A strong sentiment among the elites was the necessity for compulsory public education, so that the new electorate could understand and handle its duties. Every country developed a sense of national origins – the historical accuracy was less important than the motivation toward patriotism. <a href="/wiki/Universal_access_to_education" title="Universal access to education">Universal compulsory education</a> was extended as well to girls, at least at the elementary level. By the 1890s, strong movements emerged in some countries, including France, Germany and the United States, to extend compulsory education to the secondary level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideological_coalitions">Ideological coalitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Ideological coalitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bakunin_speaking.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1721" data-file-width="1263" decoding="async" height="259" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Bakunin_speaking.png/190px-Bakunin_speaking.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Bakunin_speaking.png/285px-Bakunin_speaking.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Bakunin_speaking.png/380px-Bakunin_speaking.png 2x" width="190"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bakunin_speaking.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Bakunin" title="Mikhail Bakunin">Mikhail Bakunin</a> speaking to members of the <a href="/wiki/International_Workingmen%27s_Association" title="International Workingmen's Association">International Workingmen's Association</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Basel_Congress_(1869)" title="Basel Congress (1869)">Basel Congress</a> in 1869</div></div></div>
<p>After the defeat of revolutionary France, the great powers tried to restore the situation which existed before 1789. In 1815 at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>, the major powers of Europe managed to produce a peaceful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balance_of_power_in_international_relations" title="Balance of power in international relations">balance of power</a> among the various European empires. This was known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metternich" title="Metternich">Metternich</a> system. The powerbase of their support was the aristocracy, with its great landed wealth and control of the government, the church, and the military in most countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> However, their reactionary efforts were unable to stop the spread of revolutionary movements: the middle classes had been deeply influenced by the ideals of the French revolution, and the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> brought important economical and social changes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup>
</p><p>Radical intellectuals looked to the <a href="/wiki/Working_class" title="Working class">working classes</a> for a base for socialist, communist and <a href="/wiki/Anarchism" title="Anarchism">anarchistic</a> ideas. Widely influential was the 1848 pamphlet by <a href="/wiki/Karl_Marx" title="Karl Marx">Karl Marx</a> and <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Engels" title="Friedrich Engels">Friedrich Engels</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Communist_Manifesto" title="The Communist Manifesto">The Communist Manifesto</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup>
</p><p>The middle classes and businessmen promoted liberalism, free trade and capitalism. Aristocratic elements concentrated in government service, the military and the established churches. Nationalist movements (in Germany, Italy, Poland, Hungary, and elsewhere) called upon the "racial" unity (which usually meant a common language and an imagined common ethnicity) to seek national unification and/or liberation from foreign rule. As a result, the period between 1815 and 1871 saw a large number of revolutionary attempts and independence wars. Greece successfully revolted against Ottoman rule in the 1820s. European diplomats and intellectuals saw the Greek struggle for independence, with its accounts of Turkish atrocities, in a romantic light.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="France_under_Napoleon_III">France under Napoleon III</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: France under Napoleon III">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Second_French_Empire" title="Second French Empire">Second French Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barricade_Voltaire_Lenoir_Commune_Paris_1871.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1532" data-file-width="2256" decoding="async" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Barricade_Voltaire_Lenoir_Commune_Paris_1871.jpg/220px-Barricade_Voltaire_Lenoir_Commune_Paris_1871.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Barricade_Voltaire_Lenoir_Commune_Paris_1871.jpg/330px-Barricade_Voltaire_Lenoir_Commune_Paris_1871.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Barricade_Voltaire_Lenoir_Commune_Paris_1871.jpg/440px-Barricade_Voltaire_Lenoir_Commune_Paris_1871.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Barricade_Voltaire_Lenoir_Commune_Paris_1871.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Paris_Commune" title="Paris Commune">Paris Commune</a>, 1871.</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Napoleon_III" title="Napoleon III">Napoleon III</a>, nephew of Napoleon I, parlayed his famous name and to widespread popularity across France. He returned from exile in 1848, promising to stabilize the chaotic political situation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> He was elected president and maneuvered successfully to name himself Emperor, a move approved later by a large majority of the French electorate. The first part of his Imperial term brought many important reforms, facilitated by Napoleon's control of the lawmaking body, the government, and the <a href="/wiki/French_Armed_Forces" title="French Armed Forces">French Armed Forces</a>. Hundreds of old Republican leaders were arrested and deported. Napoleon controlled the media and censored the news. In compensation for the loss of freedom, Napoleon gave the people new hospitals and asylums, beautified and modernized Paris, and built a modern railroad and transportation system that dramatically improved commerce, and helped the many small farmers as well. The economy grew, but industrialization was not as rapid as Britain, and France depended largely on small family-oriented firms as opposed to the large companies that were emerging in the United States and Germany. France was on the winning side in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> (1854–56), but after 1858 Napoleon's foreign-policy was less and less successful. He antagonized Great Britain and failed to appreciate the danger of war with Prussia. Foreign-policy blunders finally destroyed his reign in 1870–71. He gained worldwide attention for his aggressive foreign policy in Europe, Mexico, and worldwide. He helped in the unification of Italy by fighting the <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian Empire</a> and joined the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> on the side of the United Kingdom to defend the Ottoman Empire against Russia. His empire collapsed after being defeated in the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup>
</p><p>France became a republic, but until the 1880s there was a strong popular demand for return to monarchy. That never happened because of the blunders made by the available monarchs. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Catholicism_in_France" title="Anti-Catholicism in France">Hostility to the Catholic Church</a> became a major issue, as France battle between secular and religious forces well into the 20th century, with the secular elements usually more successful. The <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">French Third Republic</a> emerged in 1871, was on the winning side of the first world war, and was finally overthrown when it was defeated in 1940 in World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Calatafimi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Battle_of_Calatafimi.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Calatafimi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Battle_of_Calatafimi.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Calatafimi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Battle_of_Calatafimi.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Calatafimi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Calatafimi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Garibaldi" title="Giuseppe Garibaldi">Giuseppe Garibaldi</a>'s redshirts during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Calatafimi" title="Battle of Calatafimi">Battle of Calatafimi</a>, part of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Unification" title="Italian Unification">Italian Unification</a>.</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_powers">Major powers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Major powers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="wikitable">

</td></tr>

</td></tr>

<td><a class="extiw" href="//archive.org/details/americanannualc22unkngoog" title="iarchive:americanannualc22unkngoog"><i>Appleton Annual Cyclopedia: 1877</i> (1878) p. 281</a>

<p>Most European states had become <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional</a> (rather than absolute) monarchies by 1871, and Germany and Italy merged many small city-states to become united nation-states. Germany in particular increasingly dominated the continent in terms of economics and political power. Meanwhile, on a global scale, Great Britain, with its far-flung <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, unmatched Royal Navy, and powerful bankers, became the world's first global power. The sun never set on its territories, while an informal empire operated through British financiers, entrepreneurs, traders and engineers who established operations in many countries, and largely dominated Latin America. The British were especially famous for financing and constructing railways around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R68588,_Otto_von_Bismarck.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="538" decoding="async" height="253" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R68588%2C_Otto_von_Bismarck.jpg/170px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R68588%2C_Otto_von_Bismarck.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R68588%2C_Otto_von_Bismarck.jpg/255px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R68588%2C_Otto_von_Bismarck.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R68588%2C_Otto_von_Bismarck.jpg/340px-Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R68588%2C_Otto_von_Bismarck.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_Bild_183-R68588,_Otto_von_Bismarck.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck" title="Otto von Bismarck">Otto von Bismarck</a>, Chancellor of Germany</div></div></div>
<h4><span id="Bismarck.27s_Germany"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Bismarck's_Germany">Bismarck's Germany</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Bismarck's Germany">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/North_German_Confederation" title="North German Confederation">North German Confederation</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a></div>
<p>From his base in Prussia, <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck" title="Otto von Bismarck">Otto von Bismarck</a> in the 1860s engineered a series of short, decisive wars, that <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Germany" title="Unification of Germany">unified most of the German states</a> (excluding Austria) into a powerful <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> under Prussian leadership. He humiliated France in the process, but kept on good terms with Austria-Hungary. With that accomplished by 1871 he then skillfully used <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_power_(international_relations)" title="Balance of power (international relations)">balance of power</a> diplomacy to preserve Germany's new role and keep Europe at peace. The new <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> industrialized rapidly and challenged Britain for economic leadership. Bismarck disliked colonies but public and elite opinion forced him to build an overseas empire. He was removed from office in 1890 by an aggressive young Kaiser <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_II,_German_Emperor" title="Wilhelm II, German Emperor">Wilhelm II</a>, who pursued a disruptive foreign policy that polarized Europe into rival camps. These rival camps went to war with each other in 1914.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Austrian_and_Russian_empires">Austrian and Russian empires</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Austrian and Russian empires">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austrian Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a></div>
<p>The power of nationalism to create new states was irresistible in the 19th century, and the process could lead to collapse in the absence of a strong nationalism. <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> had the advantage of size, but multiple disadvantages. There were rivals on four sides, its finances were unstable, the population was fragmented into multiple ethnicities and languages that served as the bases for separatist nationalisms. It had a large army with good forts, but its industrial base was thin. Its naval resources were so minimal that it did not attempt to build an overseas empire. It did have the advantage of good diplomats, typified by <a href="/wiki/Klemens_von_Metternich" title="Klemens von Metternich">Metternich (Foreign Minister 1809–1848, Prime Minister, 1821–1848))</a>. They employed a grand strategy for survival that balanced out different forces, set up buffer zones, and kept the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hapsburg_empire" title="Hapsburg empire">Hapsburg empire</a> going despite wars with the Ottomans, Frederick the Great, Napoleon and Bismarck, until the final disaster of the First World War. The Empire overnight disintegrated into multiple states based on ethnic nationalism and the principle of self-determination.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> likewise brought together a multitude of languages and cultures, so that its military defeat in the First World War led to multiple splits that created independent Finland, Latvia, Lithuania, Estonia, and Poland, and for a brief spell, independent Ukraine, Armenia, Georgia, and Azerbaijan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Growth_of_European_armies_1871_to_1904">Growth of European armies 1871 to 1904</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: Growth of European armies 1871 to 1904">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Imperialism">Imperialism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: Imperialism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_Empires" title="Colonial Empires">Colonial Empires</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_colonialism" title="History of colonialism">History of colonialism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">Habsburg Monarchy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French colonial empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch Empire</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_colonial_empire" title="Italian colonial empire">Italian colonial empire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/German_colonial_empire" title="German colonial empire">German colonial empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Afrikakonferenz.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="293" data-file-width="381" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Afrikakonferenz.jpg/220px-Afrikakonferenz.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Afrikakonferenz.jpg/330px-Afrikakonferenz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5c/Afrikakonferenz.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Afrikakonferenz.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Berlin_Conference_(1884)" title="Berlin Conference (1884)">Berlin Conference (1884)</a> headed by <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck" title="Otto von Bismarck">Otto von Bismarck</a> that regulated European colonization in Africa during the <a href="/wiki/New_Imperialism" title="New Imperialism">New Imperialism</a> period</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonial_empires" title="Colonial empires">Colonial empires</a> were the product of the European <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a> from the 15th century. The initial impulse behind these dispersed maritime empires and those that followed was trade, driven by the new ideas and the capitalism that grew out of the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>. Both the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> quickly grew into the first global political and economic systems with territories spread around the world.
</p><p>Subsequent major European colonial empires included the <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Empire" title="Dutch Empire">Dutch</a>, and <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British</a> empires. The latter, consolidated during the period of British maritime hegemony in the 19th century, became the largest empire in history because of the improved ocean transportation technologies of the time as well as electronic communication through the telegraph, cable, and radio. At its height in 1920, the British Empire covered a quarter of the Earth's land area and comprised a quarter of its population. Other European countries, such as <a href="/wiki/Belgian_colonial_empire" title="Belgian colonial empire">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_colonial_empire" title="German colonial empire">Germany</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_colonial_empire" title="Italian colonial empire">Italy</a>, pursued colonial empires as well (mostly in Africa), but they were smaller. Ignoring the oceans, Russia built its <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> through conquest by land in Eastern Europe, and Asia.
</p><p>By the mid-19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> had declined enough to become a target for other global powers (see <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Balkans" title="History of the Balkans">History of the Balkans</a>). This instigated the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> in 1854 and began a tenser period of minor clashes among the globe-spanning empires of Europe that eventually set the stage for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a>. In the second half of the 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sardinia" title="Kingdom of Sardinia">Kingdom of Sardinia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a> carried out a series of wars that resulted in the creation of Italy and Germany as nation-states, significantly changing the balance of power in Europe. From 1870, <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck" title="Otto von Bismarck">Otto von Bismarck</a> engineered a German hegemony of Europe that put France in a critical situation. It slowly rebuilt its relationships, seeking alliances with Russia and Britain to control the growing power of Germany. In this way, two opposing sides – the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Alliance_(1882)" title="Triple Alliance (1882)">Triple Alliance of 1882</a> (Germany, Austria-Hungary and Italy) and the <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a> of 1907 (Britain, France and Russia) – formed in Europe, improving their military forces and alliances year-by-year.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quarto_Stato.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3841" data-file-width="6897" decoding="async" height="123" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Quarto_Stato.jpg/220px-Quarto_Stato.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Quarto_Stato.jpg/330px-Quarto_Stato.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Quarto_Stato.jpg/440px-Quarto_Stato.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quarto_Stato.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Fourth_Estate_(painting)" title="The Fourth Estate (painting)">The Fourth Estate (painting)</a> by <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Pellizza_da_Volpedo" title="Giuseppe Pellizza da Volpedo">Giuseppe Pellizza da Volpedo</a>.</div></div></div>
<h2><span id="1914.E2.80.931945:_two_world_wars"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1914–1945:_two_world_wars">1914–1945: two world wars</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: 1914–1945: two world wars">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">Interwar period</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interwar_international_relations" title="Interwar international relations">Interwar international relations</a>, and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_Europe_alliances_1914-en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="593" data-file-width="1002" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Map_Europe_alliances_1914-en.svg/320px-Map_Europe_alliances_1914-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Map_Europe_alliances_1914-en.svg/480px-Map_Europe_alliances_1914-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Map_Europe_alliances_1914-en.svg/640px-Map_Europe_alliances_1914-en.svg.png 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_Europe_alliances_1914-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rival military coalitions in 1914: <a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a> in green; <a href="/wiki/Triple_Alliance_(1882)" title="Triple Alliance (1882)">Triple Alliance</a> in brown.</div></div></div>
<p>German-American historian <a href="/wiki/Konrad_Jarausch" title="Konrad Jarausch">Konrad Jarausch</a>, asked if he agreed that "the European record of the past century [was] just one gigantic catastrophe", argues:
</p>
<dl><dd>It is true that the first half of the 20th century was full of internecine warfare, economic depression, ethnic cleansing and racist genocide that killed tens of millions of people, more than any other period in human history. But looking only at the disasters creates an incomplete perception, because the second half of the century witnessed a much more positive development in spite of the Cold War. After the defeat of Fascism in 1945, the peaceful revolution of 1989/90 also liberated the East from Communist control in a quite unexpected fashion. As a result, Europeans generally live more free, prosperous and healthy lives than ever before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>The "<a href="/wiki/Short_twentieth_century" title="Short twentieth century">short twentieth century</a>", from 1914 to 1991, included the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. The First World War used modern technology to kill millions of soldiers. Victory by Britain, France, the United States and other allies drastically changed the map of Europe, ending four major land empires (the Russian, German, Austro-Hungarian and Ottoman empires) and leading to the creation of nation-states across Central and Eastern Europe. The <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a> in Russia led to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> (1917–1991) and the rise of the international communist movement. Widespread economic prosperity was typical of the period before 1914, and 1920–1929. After the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> in 1929, however, democracy collapsed in most of Europe. <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>'s <a href="/wiki/National_Fascist_Party" title="National Fascist Party">National Fascist Party</a> took control in <a href="/wiki/Fascist_Italy_(1922%E2%80%931943)" title="Fascist Italy (1922–1943)">Italy</a>, and the even more aggressive <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a> led by <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> took control of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a>, 1933–45. The Second World War was fought on an even larger scale than the First war, killing many more people, and using even more advanced technology. It ended with the division of Europe between East and West, with the East under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> and the West dominated by <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>. The two sides engaged in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, with actual conflict taking place not in Europe but in Asia in the Korean War and the Vietnam War. The Imperial system collapsed. The remaining <a href="/wiki/Colonial_empire" title="Colonial empire">colonial empires</a> ended through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decolonisation" title="Decolonisation">decolonisation</a> of European rule in Africa and Asia. The <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989" title="Revolutions of 1989">fall of Soviet Communism</a> (1989–1991) left the West dominant and enabled the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reunification_of_Germany" title="Reunification of Germany">reunification of Germany</a>. It accelerated the process of a <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a> to include Eastern Europe. The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> continues today, but with German economic dominance. Since the worldwide <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a> of 2008, European growth has been slow, and financial crises have hit Greece and other countries. Modern-day Russia is weaker by military might, compared to when it was a superpower as a part of the Soviet Union, but has retained its historical status as both a <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great power</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Regional_power" title="Regional power">regional power</a>, confronting Ukraine and other post-Soviet states.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=59" title="Edit section: World War I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Home_front_during_World_War_I" title="Home front during World War I">Home front during World War I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_history_of_World_War_I" title="Diplomatic history of World War I">Diplomatic history of World War I</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_World_War_I" title="Economic history of World War I">Economic history of World War I</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trencheswwi2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="595" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Trencheswwi2.jpg/220px-Trencheswwi2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Trencheswwi2.jpg/330px-Trencheswwi2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Trencheswwi2.jpg/440px-Trencheswwi2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trencheswwi2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Trenches and sand bags were defences against machine guns and artillery on the Western Front, 1914–1918</div></div></div>
<p>After the relative peace of most of the 19th century, the rivalry between European powers, compounded by a rising nationalism among ethnic groups, exploded in August 1914, when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a> started.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> Over 65 million European soldiers were mobilised from 1914 to 1918; 20 million soldiers and civilians died, and 21 million were seriously wounded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> On one side were Germany, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> (the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a>/<a href="/wiki/Triple_Alliance_(1882)" title="Triple Alliance (1882)">Triple Alliance</a>), while on the other side stood <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Triple_Entente" title="Triple Entente">Triple Entente</a></i> – the coalition of France, Britain and Russia, which were joined by Italy in 1915, Romania in 1916 and by the United States in 1917. The <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a> involved especially brutal combat without any territorial gains by either side. Single battles like <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Verdun" title="Battle of Verdun">Verdun</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Somme" title="Battle of the Somme">Somme</a> killed hundreds of thousands of men while leaving the stalemate unchanged. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heavy_artillery" title="Heavy artillery">Heavy artillery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Machine_gun" title="Machine gun">machine guns</a> caused most of the casualties, supplemented by <a href="/wiki/Chemical_weapons_in_World_War_I" title="Chemical weapons in World War I">poison gas</a>. Czarist Russia collapsed in the <a href="/wiki/February_Revolution" title="February Revolution">February Revolution</a> of 1917 and Germany claimed victory on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Eastern Front (World War I)">Eastern Front</a>. After eight months of <a href="/wiki/Russian_Republic" title="Russian Republic">liberal rule</a>, the <a href="/wiki/October_Revolution" title="October Revolution">October Revolution</a> brought <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bolsheviks" title="Bolsheviks">Bolsheviks</a> to power, leading to the creation of the Soviet Union in place of the disintegrated Russian Empire. With <a href="/wiki/American_entry_into_World_War_I" title="American entry into World War I">American entry into the war</a> in 1917 on the Allied side, and the failure of <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Days_Offensive" title="Hundred Days Offensive">Germany's spring 1918 offensive</a>, Germany had run out of manpower, while an average of 10,000 American troops were arriving in France every day in the summer of 1918. Germany's allies, <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, surrendered and dissolved, followed by Germany on 11 November 1918.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> The victors forced Germany to assume responsibility for the conflict and pay war reparations.
</p><p>One factor in determining the outcome of the war was that the Allies had significantly more economic resources they could spend on the war. One estimate (using 1913 US dollars) is that the Allies spent $58 billion on the war and the Central Powers only $25 billion. Among the Allies, Britain spent $21 billion and the U.S. $17 billion; among the Central Powers Germany spent $20 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paris_Peace_Conference">Paris Peace Conference</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=60" title="Edit section: Paris Peace Conference">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">Paris Peace Conference, 1919</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:William_Orpen_%E2%80%93_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors,_Versailles_1919,_Ausschnitt.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="2238" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/William_Orpen_%E2%80%93_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors%2C_Versailles_1919%2C_Ausschnitt.jpg/450px-William_Orpen_%E2%80%93_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors%2C_Versailles_1919%2C_Ausschnitt.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/William_Orpen_%E2%80%93_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors%2C_Versailles_1919%2C_Ausschnitt.jpg/675px-William_Orpen_%E2%80%93_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors%2C_Versailles_1919%2C_Ausschnitt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/William_Orpen_%E2%80%93_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors%2C_Versailles_1919%2C_Ausschnitt.jpg/900px-William_Orpen_%E2%80%93_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors%2C_Versailles_1919%2C_Ausschnitt.jpg 2x" width="450"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:William_Orpen_%E2%80%93_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors,_Versailles_1919,_Ausschnitt.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Detail from <a href="/wiki/William_Orpen" title="William Orpen">William Orpen</a>'s painting <i>The Signing of Peace in the Hall of Mirrors, Versailles, 28 June 1919</i>, showing the signing of the peace treaty by a minor German official opposite to the representatives of the winning powers.</div></div></div>
<p>The world war was settled by the victors at the Paris Peace Conference in 1919. Two dozen nations sent delegations, and there were many nongovernmental groups, but the defeated powers were not invited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>
</p><p>The "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Big_Four_(World_War_I)" title="The Big Four (World War I)">Big Four</a>" were President <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Woodrow_Wilson" title="Presidency of Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a> of the United States, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/David_Lloyd_George" title="David Lloyd George">David Lloyd George</a> of Great Britain, <a href="/wiki/Georges_Clemenceau" title="Georges Clemenceau">Georges Clemenceau</a> of France, and, of least importance, Italian Prime Minister <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vittorio_Orlando" title="Vittorio Orlando">Vittorio Orlando</a>.  Each has a large staff of experts. They met together informally 145 times and made all the major decisions, which in turn were ratified by the others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup>
</p><p>The major decisions were the creation of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>; the six peace treaties with defeated enemies, most notable the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> with Germany; the awarding of German and Ottoman overseas possessions as <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_mandate" title="League of Nations mandate">"mandates"</a>, chiefly to Britain and France; and the drawing of new national boundaries (sometimes with plebiscites) to better reflect the forces of nationalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Big Four implemented sweeping changes to the <a href="/wiki/Political_geography" title="Political geography">political geography</a> of the world. Most famously, the Treaty of Versailles itself weakened <a href="/wiki/Reichswehr" title="Reichswehr">Germany's military power</a> and placed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_Guilt_Clause" title="War Guilt Clause">full blame for the war</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_War_I_reparations" title="World War I reparations">costly reparations</a> on its shoulders – the humiliation and resentment in Germany was probably one of the causes of Nazi success and indirectly a <a href="/wiki/Causes_of_World_War_II" title="Causes of World War II">cause of World War II</a>.
</p><p>At the insistence of President Wilson, the Big Four required the <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Second Polish Republic</a> to sign a treaty on 28 June 1919 that guaranteed <a href="/wiki/Minority_rights" title="Minority rights">minority rights</a> in the new nation. Poland signed under protest, and made little effort to enforce the specified rights for <a href="/wiki/German_minority_in_Poland" title="German minority in Poland">Germans</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland" title="History of the Jews in Poland">Jews</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians_in_Poland" title="Ukrainians in Poland">Ukrainians</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_minorities_in_Poland" title="Ethnic minorities in Poland">minorities</a>. Similar treaties were signed by <a href="/wiki/First_Czechoslovak_Republic" title="First Czechoslovak Republic">Czechoslovakia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania" title="Kingdom of Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Greece" title="Kingdom of Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/First_Austrian_Republic" title="First Austrian Republic">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary_(1920%E2%80%931946)" title="Kingdom of Hungary (1920–1946)">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bulgaria" title="Kingdom of Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, and later by Latvia, Estonia and Lithuania. Finland and Germany were not asked to sign a <a href="/wiki/Minority_Treaties" title="Minority Treaties">minority rights treaty</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interwar">Interwar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=61" title="Edit section: Interwar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I" title="Aftermath of World War I">Aftermath of World War I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">Interwar period</a>, and <a href="/wiki/International_relations_(1919%E2%80%931939)" title="International relations (1919–1939)">International relations (1919–1939)</a></div>
