<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_Europe_1923-en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="704" data-file-width="1037" decoding="async" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Map_Europe_1923-en.svg/320px-Map_Europe_1923-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Map_Europe_1923-en.svg/480px-Map_Europe_1923-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Map_Europe_1923-en.svg/640px-Map_Europe_1923-en.svg.png 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_Europe_1923-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_border_changes_(1914%E2%80%93present)" title="List of national border changes (1914–present)">territorial changes in Europe</a> after World War<span class="nowrap"> </span>I (as of 1923)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sweden_Vaxholm_1938.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="805" data-file-width="1200" decoding="async" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sweden_Vaxholm_1938.jpg/320px-Sweden_Vaxholm_1938.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sweden_Vaxholm_1938.jpg/480px-Sweden_Vaxholm_1938.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Sweden_Vaxholm_1938.jpg/640px-Sweden_Vaxholm_1938.jpg 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sweden_Vaxholm_1938.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>People gathered at sport event in 1938 (Sweden).</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palatinus_Strandf%C3%BCrd%C5%91._Fortepan_78086.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2938" data-file-width="4370" decoding="async" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Palatinus_Strandf%C3%BCrd%C5%91._Fortepan_78086.jpg/320px-Palatinus_Strandf%C3%BCrd%C5%91._Fortepan_78086.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Palatinus_Strandf%C3%BCrd%C5%91._Fortepan_78086.jpg/480px-Palatinus_Strandf%C3%BCrd%C5%91._Fortepan_78086.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Palatinus_Strandf%C3%BCrd%C5%91._Fortepan_78086.jpg/640px-Palatinus_Strandf%C3%BCrd%C5%91._Fortepan_78086.jpg 2x" width="320"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palatinus_Strandf%C3%BCrd%C5%91._Fortepan_78086.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Europeans from various countries relaxing in wave pool in Hungary in 1939 just before the Second World War. Visible inscriptions in numerous languages.</div></div></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a> (1919) the winners recognised the new states (<a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a>, Hungary, Austria, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Yugoslavia" title="Kingdom of Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, Finland, Estonia, Latvia, Lithuania) created in central Europe from the defunct German, Austro-Hungarian and Russian empires, based on national (ethnic) self-determination. It was a peaceful era with a few small wars before 1922 such as the <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian%E2%80%93Soviet_War" title="Ukrainian–Soviet War">Ukrainian–Soviet War</a> (1917–1921) and the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War" title="Polish–Soviet War">Polish–Soviet War</a> (1919–1921). Prosperity was widespread, and the major cities sponsored a youth culture called the "<a href="/wiki/Roaring_Twenties" title="Roaring Twenties">Roaring Twenties</a>" or "<a href="/wiki/Jazz_Age" title="Jazz Age">Jazz Age</a>" that was often featured in the cinema, which attracted very large audiences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Allied victory in the First World War seemed to mark the triumph of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Liberalism" title="History of Liberalism">liberalism</a>, not just in the Allied countries themselves, but also in Germany and in the new states of Eastern Europe, as well as Japan. Authoritarian militarism as typified by Germany had been defeated and discredited. Historian Martin Blinkhorn argues that the liberal themes were ascendant in terms of "<a href="/wiki/Cultural_pluralism" title="Cultural pluralism">cultural pluralism</a>, religious and ethnic toleration, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_self-determination" title="National self-determination">national self-determination</a>, <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free-market economics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative</a> and <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">responsible government</a>, <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trade_unions_in_Europe" title="Trade unions in Europe">unionism</a>, and the peaceful settlement of international disputes through a new body, the League of Nations."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup> However, as early as 1917, the emerging liberal order was being challenged by the new <a href="/wiki/Communist_International" title="Communist International">communist movement</a> taking inspiration from the Russian Revolution. Communist revolts were beaten back everywhere else, but they did succeed in Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fascism_and_authoritarianism">Fascism and authoritarianism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=62" title="Edit section: Fascism and authoritarianism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/European_interwar_dictatorships" title="European interwar dictatorships">European interwar dictatorships</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fascist_Italy_(1922%E2%80%931943)" title="Fascist Italy (1922–1943)">Fascist Italy (1922–1943)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a></div>
<p>Italy adopted an authoritarian dictatorship known as <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">Fascism</a> in 1922; it became a model for Hitler in Germany and for right wing elements in other countries. Historian <a href="/wiki/Stanley_G._Payne" title="Stanley G. Payne">Stanley G. Payne</a> says <a href="/wiki/Italian_fascism" title="Italian fascism">Italian fascism</a> was:
</p>
<dl><dd>A primarily political dictatorship....The <a href="/wiki/National_Fascist_Party" title="National Fascist Party">Fascist Party</a> itself had become almost completely bureaucratized and subservient to, not dominant over, the state itself. Big business, industry, and finance retained extensive autonomy, particularly in the early years. The armed forces also enjoyed considerable autonomy....The <a href="/wiki/Blackshirts" title="Blackshirts">Fascist militia</a> was placed under military control....The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Italy" title="Judiciary of Italy">judicial system</a> was left largely intact and relatively autonomous as well. The police continued to be directed by state officials and were not taken over by party leaders...nor was a major new police elite created....There was never any question of bringing the Church under overall subservience.... Sizable sectors of <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Italy" title="Culture of Italy">Italian cultural life</a> retained extensive autonomy, and no major state propaganda-and-culture ministry existed....The Mussolini regime was neither especially sanguinary nor particularly repressive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Authoritarian regimes replaced democracy in the 1930s in <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Estado_Novo_(Portugal)" title="Estado Novo (Portugal)">Portugal</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austrofascism" title="Austrofascism">Austria</a>, Poland, <a href="/wiki/4th_of_August_Regime" title="4th of August Regime">Greece</a>, the Baltic countries and <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Francoist Spain</a>. By 1940, there were only four liberal democracies left on the European continent: <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a>, Finland, Switzerland and Sweden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Great_Depression:_1929.E2.80.931939"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Depression:_1929–1939">Great Depression: 1929–1939</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=63" title="Edit section: Great Depression: 1929–1939">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a></div>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">Wall Street Crash of 1929</a>, nearly the whole world sank into a <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, as money stopped flowing from New York to Europe, prices fell, profits fell, and unemployment soared. The worst hit sectors included heavy industry, export-oriented agriculture, mining and lumbering, and construction. World trade fell by two-thirds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup>
</p><p>Liberalism and democracy were discredited. In most of Europe, as well as in Japan and most of Latin America, nation after nation turned to dictators and authoritarian regimes. The most momentous change of government came when Hitler and his <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler%27s_rise_to_power" title="Adolf Hitler's rise to power">Nazis took power in Germany</a> in 1933. The main institution that was meant to bring stability was the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>, created in 1919. However the League failed to resolve any major crises and by 1938 it was no longer a major player. The League was undermined by the bellicosity of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Imperial_Japan" title="Imperial Japan">Imperial Japan</a>, the Soviet Union, and <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Mussolini's</a> Italy, and by the non-participation of the United States. By 1937 it was largely ignored.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup>
</p><p>A <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">major civil war</a> took place in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spain</a>, with the nationalists winning. The League of Nations was helpless as <a href="/wiki/Second_Italo-Ethiopian_War" title="Second Italo-Ethiopian War">Italy conquered Ethiopia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Japanese invasion of Manchuria">Japan seized Manchuria</a> in 1931 and <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">took over most of China</a> starting in 1937.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Milicianas_CNT-FAI.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="364" data-file-width="565" decoding="async" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Milicianas_CNT-FAI.png/200px-Milicianas_CNT-FAI.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Milicianas_CNT-FAI.png/300px-Milicianas_CNT-FAI.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Milicianas_CNT-FAI.png/400px-Milicianas_CNT-FAI.png 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Milicianas_CNT-FAI.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Federaci%C3%B3n_Anarquista_Ib%C3%A9rica" title="Federación Anarquista Ibérica">FAI</a> milicia during <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Revolution_of_1936" title="Spanish Revolution of 1936">Spanish Social Revolution</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a> (1936–1939) was marked by numerous small battles and sieges, and many atrocities, until the rebels (the <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_faction_(Spanish_Civil_War)" title="Nationalist faction (Spanish Civil War)">Nationalist faction</a>), led by <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a>, won in 1939. There was military intervention as Italy sent land forces, and Germany sent smaller elite air force and armoured units to the Nationalists. The Soviet Union sold armaments to the leftist <a href="/wiki/Republican_faction_(Spanish_Civil_War)" title="Republican faction (Spanish Civil War)">Republican faction</a> on the other side, while the Communist parties in numerous countries sent soldiers to the "<a href="/wiki/International_Brigades" title="International Brigades">International Brigades</a>." The civil war did not escalate into a larger conflict, but did become a worldwide ideological battleground that pitted the left, the communist movement and many liberals against Catholics, conservatives, and fascists. Britain, France and the US remained neutral and refused to sell military supplies to either side. Worldwide there was a decline in pacifism and a growing sense that another world war was imminent, and that it would be worth fighting for.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=64" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Causes_of_World_War_II" title="Causes of World War II">Causes of World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diplomatic_history_of_World_War_II" title="Diplomatic history of World War II">Diplomatic history of World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Home_front_during_World_War_II" title="Home front during World War II">Home front during World War II</a>, and <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">The Holocaust</a></div>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">Munich Agreement</a> of 1938, Britain and France adopted a policy of <a href="/wiki/Appeasement" title="Appeasement">appeasement</a> as they gave <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hitler" title="Hitler">Hitler</a> what he wanted out of Czechoslovakia in the hope that it would bring peace. It did not. In 1939 <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_Czechoslovakia_(1938%E2%80%931945)" title="Occupation of Czechoslovakia (1938–1945)">Germany took over the rest of Czechoslovakia</a> and appeasement policies gave way to hurried rearmament as Hitler next turned his attention to Poland.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_N_1576_Bild-003,_Warschau,_Bettelnde_Kinder.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="514" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Bundesarchiv_N_1576_Bild-003%2C_Warschau%2C_Bettelnde_Kinder.jpg/220px-Bundesarchiv_N_1576_Bild-003%2C_Warschau%2C_Bettelnde_Kinder.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Bundesarchiv_N_1576_Bild-003%2C_Warschau%2C_Bettelnde_Kinder.jpg/330px-Bundesarchiv_N_1576_Bild-003%2C_Warschau%2C_Bettelnde_Kinder.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Bundesarchiv_N_1576_Bild-003%2C_Warschau%2C_Bettelnde_Kinder.jpg/440px-Bundesarchiv_N_1576_Bild-003%2C_Warschau%2C_Bettelnde_Kinder.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_N_1576_Bild-003,_Warschau,_Bettelnde_Kinder.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Starving Jewish children in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto" title="Warsaw Ghetto">Warsaw Ghetto</a> (1940–1943).</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_1944.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="787" data-file-width="1181" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Warsaw_1944.jpg/220px-Warsaw_1944.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Warsaw_1944.jpg/330px-Warsaw_1944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Warsaw_1944.jpg/440px-Warsaw_1944.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_1944.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The fight against German Nazis during the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising" title="Warsaw Uprising">Warsaw Uprising</a> in 1944.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AmericanAndSovietAtElbe.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="300" data-file-width="354" decoding="async" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/AmericanAndSovietAtElbe.jpg/220px-AmericanAndSovietAtElbe.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/AmericanAndSovietAtElbe.jpg/330px-AmericanAndSovietAtElbe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1b/AmericanAndSovietAtElbe.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AmericanAndSovietAtElbe.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>American and Soviet troops <a href="/wiki/Elbe_Day" title="Elbe Day">meet in April 1945</a>, east of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elbe_River" title="Elbe River">Elbe River</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>After allying with Japan in the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Comintern_Pact" title="Anti-Comintern Pact">Anti-Comintern Pact</a> and then also with <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>'s Italy in the "<a href="/wiki/Pact_of_Steel" title="Pact of Steel">Pact of Steel</a>", and finally signing a <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov–Ribbentrop Pact">non-aggression treaty</a> with the Soviet Union in August 1939, Hitler launched the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> on 1 September 1939 by <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">attacking Poland</a>. To his surprise Britain and France declared war on Germany, but there was little fighting during the "<a href="/wiki/Phoney_War" title="Phoney War">Phoney War</a>" period. War began in earnest in spring 1940 with the successful Blitzkrieg conquests of Denmark, Norway, the Low Countries, and France. Britain remained alone but refused to negotiate, and defeated Germany's air attacks in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">Battle of Britain</a>. Hitler's goal was to control Eastern Europe but because of his failure to defeat Britain and the Italian failures in <a href="/wiki/North_African_campaign" title="North African campaign">North Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balkans_campaign_(World_War_II)" title="Balkans campaign (World War II)">the Balkans</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">great attack on the Soviet Union</a> was delayed until June 1941. Despite initial successes, the <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a> was stopped close to Moscow in December 1941.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup>
</p><p>Over the next year the tide was turned and the Germans started to suffer a series of defeats, for example in the siege of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Stalingrad</a> and at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk" title="Battle of Kursk">Kursk</a>. Meanwhile, Japan (allied to Germany and Italy since September 1940) attacked Britain and the United States on 7 December 1941; Germany then completed its over-extension by declaring war on the United States. War raged between the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis Powers</a> (Germany, Italy, and Japan) and the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied Forces</a> (British Empire, Soviet Union, and the United States). The Allied Forces won in North Africa, <a href="/wiki/Allied_invasion_of_Italy" title="Allied invasion of Italy">invaded Italy</a> in 1943, and <a href="/wiki/Liberation_of_France" title="Liberation of France">recaptured France</a> in 1944. In the spring of 1945 Germany itself was <a href="/wiki/East_Prussian_offensive" title="East Prussian offensive">invaded from the east by the Soviet Union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Allied_invasion_of_Germany" title="Western Allied invasion of Germany">from the west by the other Allies</a>. As the Red Army conquered the <a href="/wiki/Reichstag_building" title="Reichstag building">Reichstag</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin" title="Battle of Berlin">Battle of Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Adolf_Hitler" title="Death of Adolf Hitler">Hitler committed suicide</a> and Germany surrendered in early May.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> World War II was the deadliest conflict in human history, causing <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties" title="World War II casualties">between 50 and 80 million deaths</a>, the majority of whom were civilians (approximately 38 to 55 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup>
</p><p>This period was also marked by systematic genocide. In 1942–45, separately from the war-related deaths, the <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazis</a> killed an additional number of over 11 million civilians <a href="/wiki/IBM_and_the_Holocaust" title="IBM and the Holocaust">identified through IBM-enabled censuses</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">majority of the Jews</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Porajmos" title="Porajmos">Gypsies</a> of Europe, millions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nazi_crimes_against_ethnic_Poles" title="Nazi crimes against ethnic Poles">Polish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Generalplan_Ost" title="Generalplan Ost">Soviet</a> Slavs, and also homosexuals, <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>, misfits, disabled, and political enemies. Meanwhile, in the 1930s the Soviet system of <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">forced labour</a>, <a href="/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Population transfer in the Soviet Union">expulsions</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holodomor" title="Holodomor">allegedly engineered famine</a> had a similar death toll. During and after the war millions of civilians were affected by forced population transfers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Colonization_1945.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="638" data-file-width="1438" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonization_1945.png/330px-Colonization_1945.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonization_1945.png/495px-Colonization_1945.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Colonization_1945.png/660px-Colonization_1945.png 2x" width="330"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Colonization_1945.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Western European colonial empires in Asia and Africa disintegrated after World War II (mostly dominated by British and France.)</div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cold_War_era">Cold War era<span class="anchor" id="Postwar_Europe"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=65" title="Edit section: Cold War era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Wall_1961-11-20.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="352" data-file-width="500" decoding="async" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Berlin_Wall_1961-11-20.jpg/200px-Berlin_Wall_1961-11-20.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Berlin_Wall_1961-11-20.jpg/300px-Berlin_Wall_1961-11-20.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Berlin_Wall_1961-11-20.jpg/400px-Berlin_Wall_1961-11-20.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Berlin_Wall_1961-11-20.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>East German construction workers building the Berlin Wall, 20 November 1961</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DNV_opona.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" decoding="async" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/DNV_opona.jpg/200px-DNV_opona.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/DNV_opona.jpg/300px-DNV_opona.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/DNV_opona.jpg/400px-DNV_opona.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DNV_opona.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Remains of the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iron_curtain" title="Iron curtain">Iron curtain</a>" in <a href="/wiki/Dev%C3%ADnska_Nov%C3%A1_Ves" title="Devínska Nová Ves">Devínska Nová Ves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">Bratislava</a> (Slovakia).</div></div></div>
<p>The world wars ended the pre-eminent position of Britain, France and Germany in Europe and the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a>, Europe was divided into spheres of influence between the victors of World War II, and soon became the principal zone of contention in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> between the two power blocs, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_countries" title="Western countries">Western countries</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist_bloc" title="Communist bloc">Communist bloc</a>. The United States and the majority of European liberal democracies at the time (United Kingdom, France, Italy, Netherlands, West Germany etc.) established the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> military alliance. Later, the Soviet Union and its satellites (Bulgaria, Czechoslovakia, <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>, Hungary, Poland, and Romania) in 1955 established the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a> as a counterpoint to NATO. The Warsaw Pact had a much larger ground force, but the American-French-British <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_umbrella" title="Nuclear umbrella">nuclear umbrellas</a> protected NATO.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Communist_state" title="Communist state">Communist states</a> were imposed by the Red Army in the East, while parliamentary democracy became the dominant form of government in the West. Most historians point to its success as the product of exhaustion with war and dictatorship, and the promise of continued economic prosperity. Martin Conway also adds that an important impetus came from the anti-Nazi wartime political coalitions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_recovery">Economic recovery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=66" title="Edit section: Economic recovery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a></div>
<p>The United States gave away about $20 billion in <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">Marshall Plan</a> grants and other grants and low-interest long-term loans to Western Europe, 1945 to 1951. Historian Michael J. Hogan argues that American aid was critical in stabilizing the economy and politics of Western Europe. It brought in modern management that dramatically increased productivity, and encouraged cooperation between labor and management, and among the member states. Local Communist parties were opposed, and they lost prestige and influence and a role in government. In strategic terms, says Hogan, the Marshall Plan strengthened the West against the possibility of a communist invasion or political takeover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup> However, the Marshall Plan's role in the rapid recovery has been debated. Most reject the idea that it only miraculously revived Europe, since the evidence shows that a general recovery was already under way thanks to other aid programs from the United States. Economic historians Bradford De Long and <a href="/wiki/Barry_Eichengreen" title="Barry Eichengreen">Barry Eichengreen</a> conclude it was, " History's Most Successful Structural Adjustment Program." They state:
</p>
<dl><dd>It was not large enough to have significantly accelerated recovery by financing investment, aiding the reconstruction of damaged infrastructure, or easing commodity bottlenecks. We argue, however, that the Marshall Plan did play a major role in setting the stage for post-World War II Western Europe's rapid growth. The conditions attached to Marshall Plan aid pushed European political economy in a direction that left its post World War II "<a href="/wiki/Mixed_economy" title="Mixed economy">mixed economies</a>" with more "market" and less "controls" in the mix.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marshall_Plan.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="395" data-file-width="428" decoding="async" height="323" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Marshall_Plan.png/350px-Marshall_Plan.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/53/Marshall_Plan.png 1.5x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marshall_Plan.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marshall Plan dollar amounts</div></div></div>
<p>The Soviet Union concentrated on its own recovery. It seized and transferred most of Germany's industrial plants and it exacted <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_reparations" title="World War II reparations">war reparations</a> from East Germany, Hungary, Romania, and Bulgaria, using Soviet-dominated joint enterprises. It used trading arrangements deliberately designed to favor the Soviet Union. Moscow controlled the Communist parties that ruled the satellite states, and they followed orders from the Kremlin. Historian Mark Kramer concludes:
</p>
<dl><dd>The net outflow of resources from eastern Europe to the Soviet Union was approximately $15 billion to $20 billion in the first decade after World War II, an amount roughly equal to the total aid provided by the United States to western Europe under the Marshall Plan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Western Europe began economic and then political integration, with the aim to unite the region and defend it. This process included organisations such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a>, which grew and evolved into the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solidarno%C5%9B%C4%87" title="Solidarność">Solidarność</a> movement in the 1980s weakened the <a href="/wiki/Polish_People%27s_Republic" title="Polish People's Republic">Communist government in Poland</a>. At the time the Soviet leader <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a> initiated <a href="/wiki/Perestroika" title="Perestroika">perestroika</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">glasnost</a>, which weakened Soviet influence in Europe, particularly in the USSR. In 1989 after the <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_Picnic" title="Pan-European Picnic">Pan-European Picnic</a> the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Berlin_Wall" title="Fall of the Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall came down</a> and Communist governments outside the Soviet Union were deposed. In 1990 the Federal Republic of Germany absorbed East Germany, after making large cash payments to the USSR. In 1991 the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Communist Party of the Soviet Union">Communist Party of the Soviet Union</a> in Moscow collapsed, <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">ending the USSR</a>, which split into fifteen independent states. The largest, Russia, took the Soviet Union's seat on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a>. The most violent dissolution happened in Yugoslavia, in the Balkans. Four (<a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, Croatia, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_Macedonia" title="North Macedonia">North Macedonia</a>) out of six Yugoslav republics declared independence and for most of them a violent war ensued, in some parts lasting until 1995. In 2006 Montenegro seceded and became an independent state. In the <a href="/wiki/Post%E2%80%93Cold_War_era" title="Post–Cold War era">post–Cold War era</a>, NATO and the EU have been gradually admitting most of the former members of the Warsaw Pact.
</p><p>Looking at the half century after the war historian <a href="/wiki/Walter_Laqueur" title="Walter Laqueur">Walter Lacquer</a> concluded:
</p>
<dl><dd>"The postwar generations of European elites aimed to create more democratic societies. They wanted to reduce the extremes of wealth and poverty and provide essential social services in a way that prewar generations had not. They had had quite enough of unrest and conflict. For decades many Continental societies had more or less achieved these aims and had every reason to be proud of their progress. Europe was quiet and civilized. Europe's success was based on recent painful experience: the horrors of two world wars; the lessons of dictatorship; the experiences of fascism and communism. Above all, it was based on a feeling of European identity and common values – or so it appeared at the time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>The post-war period also witnessed a significant rise in the standard of living of the Western European working class. As noted by one historical text, "within a single generation, the working classes of Western Europe came to enjoy the multiple pleasures of the consumer society."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google2_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-google2-198">[198]</a></sup>
</p><p>Western Europe's industrial nations in the 1970s were hit by a <a href="/wiki/1973%E2%80%931975_recession" title="1973–1975 recession">global economic crisis</a>. They had obsolescent heavy industry, and suddenly had to pay very high energy prices which caused sharp inflation. Some of them also had inefficient nationalized railways and heavy industries. In the important field of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Computer_Technology" title="Computer Technology">computer technology</a>, European nations lagged behind the United States. They also faced high <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_deficit" title="Government deficit">government deficits</a> and growing unrest led by militant <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">labour unions</a>. There was an urgent need for new economic directions. Germany and Sweden sought to create a social consensus behind a gradual restructuring. Germany's efforts proved highly successful. In Britain under the <a href="/wiki/Premiership_of_Margaret_Thatcher" title="Premiership of Margaret Thatcher">premiership of Margaret Thatcher</a>, the solution was shock therapy, high interest rates, austerity, and selling off inefficient corporations as well as the public housing, which was sold off to the tenants. One result was escalating social tensions in Britain, led by the militant coal miners. Thatcher eventually defeated her opponents and radically changed the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Economy of the United Kingdom">British economy</a>, but the controversy never went away as shown by the hostile demonstrations at the time of her death in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_history">Recent history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=67" title="Edit section: Recent history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Cold_War_(1979%E2%80%931985)" title="Cold War (1979–1985)">Cold War (1979–1985)</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_European_Union" title="History of the European Union">History of the European Union</a>, and <a href="/wiki/International_relations_since_1989" title="International relations since 1989">International relations since 1989</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="498" data-file-width="661" decoding="async" height="166" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg/220px-West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg/330px-West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg/440px-West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:West_and_East_Germans_at_the_Brandenburg_Gate_in_1989.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Germans standing on top of the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg_Gate" title="Brandenburg Gate">Brandenburg Gate</a>, November 1989; it would begin to be torn apart in the following days.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cold_War_border_changes.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="436" data-file-width="599" decoding="async" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Cold_War_border_changes.png/260px-Cold_War_border_changes.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Cold_War_border_changes.png/390px-Cold_War_border_changes.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Cold_War_border_changes.png/520px-Cold_War_border_changes.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cold_War_border_changes.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Changes in national boundaries after the end of the Cold War and the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="Dissolution of the Soviet Union">dissolution of the Soviet Union</a> in 1991</div></div></div>
<p>The end of the Cold War came in a series of events from 1979 to 1991, mainly in Eastern Europe. In the end, these brought the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> and the end of Soviet control over their Eastern European satellites and their worldwide network of communist parties in a friendly chain reaction from the <a href="/wiki/Pan-European_Picnic" title="Pan-European Picnic">Pan-European Picnic</a> in 1989. The finals brought the division of the Soviet Union into 15 non-communist states in 1991.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup>
Italian historian Federico Romero reports that observers at the time emphasized that:
</p>
<dl><dd>The systemic and ideological confrontation between capitalism and communism had faded away. The geopolitical partition of Europe was no more. Nuclear deterrence was morphing into a less armed, almost hypothetical version of its previous self. Superpower rivalry was rapidly wound up with cascading effects in various areas of the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup></dd></dl>
<p>Following the end of the Cold War, the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> pushed for closer integration, co-operation in foreign and home affairs, and started to increase its membership into the neutral and former communist countries. In 1993, the <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_Treaty" title="Maastricht Treaty">Maastricht Treaty</a> established the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, succeeding the EEC and furthering political co-operation. The neutral countries of Austria, Finland and Sweden acceded to the EU, and those that didn't join were tied into the EU's economic market via the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Area" title="European Economic Area">European Economic Area</a>. These countries also entered the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Agreement</a> which lifted border controls between member states.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Europa_History_90-99_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-Europa_History_90-99-202">[202]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Maastricht Treaty created a single currency for most EU members. The <i><a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a></i> was created in 1999 and replaced all previous currencies in participating states in 2002. The most notable exception to the currency union, or <i><a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">eurozone</a></i>, was the United Kingdom, which also did not sign the Schengen Agreement.
</p><p>The EU did not participate in the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_Wars" title="Yugoslav Wars">Yugoslav Wars</a>, and was divided on supporting the United States in the 2003–2011 <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a>. NATO was part of the <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%932021)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–2021)">war in Afghanistan</a>, but at a much lower level of involvement than the United States.
</p><p>In 2004, the EU <a href="/wiki/2004_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2004 enlargement of the European Union">gained 10 new members</a>. (<a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a>, which had been part of the Soviet Union; <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a>, Hungary, Poland, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a>, five former-communist countries; <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, and the divided island of <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a>.) These were followed by <a href="/wiki/2007_enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="2007 enlargement of the European Union">Bulgaria and Romania in 2007</a>. Russia's regime had interpreted these expansions as violations against NATO's promise to not expand "one inch to the east" in 1990.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> Russia engaged in a number of bilateral disputes about gas supplies with <a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> which endangered gas supplies to Europe. Russia also engaged in a <a href="/wiki/Russo-Georgian_War" title="Russo-Georgian War">minor war with Georgia</a> in 2008.
</p><p>Supported by the United States and some European countries, <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>'s government <a href="/wiki/2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unilaterally declared independence</a> from Serbia on 17 February 2008.
</p><p>Public opinion in the EU turned against enlargement, partially due to what was seen as over-eager expansion including Turkey gaining candidate status. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_establishing_a_Constitution_for_Europe" title="Treaty establishing a Constitution for Europe">European Constitution</a> was rejected <a href="/wiki/Referendums_related_to_the_European_Union" title="Referendums related to the European Union">in France and the Netherlands</a>, and then (as the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lisbon" title="Treaty of Lisbon">Treaty of Lisbon</a>) in Ireland, although a second vote passed in Ireland in 2009.
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_of_2007%E2%80%9308" title="Financial crisis of 2007–08">financial crisis of 2007–08</a> <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">affected</a> Europe, and government responded with <a href="/wiki/Anti-austerity_movement" title="Anti-austerity movement">austerity measures</a>. Limited <a href="/wiki/National_accounts" title="National accounts">ability</a> of the smaller EU nations (most notably <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Greece#2010–2018_government_debt_crisis" title="Economy of Greece">Greece</a>) to handle their debts led to social unrest, government liquidation, and financial insolvency. In May 2010, the German parliament agreed to loan 22.4 billion euros to Greece over three years, with the stipulation that Greece follow strict austerity measures. See <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_sovereign-debt_crisis" title="European sovereign-debt crisis">European sovereign-debt crisis</a>.
</p><p>Beginning in 2014, <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> has been in a <a href="/wiki/Revolution_of_Dignity" title="Revolution of Dignity">state of revolution</a> and unrest with two breakaway regions (<a href="/wiki/Donetsk" title="Donetsk">Donetsk</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lugansk" title="Lugansk">Lugansk</a>) attempting to join Russia as full <a href="/wiki/Federal_subjects_of_Russia" title="Federal subjects of Russia">federal subjects</a>. (<i>See <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russo-Ukrainian War</a>.</i>) On 16 March, a <a href="/wiki/2014_Crimean_status_referendum" title="2014 Crimean status referendum">disputed referendum</a> was held in <a href="/wiki/Crimea" title="Crimea">Crimea</a> leading to the <i>de facto</i> secession of Crimea and its largely internationally unrecognized <a href="/wiki/Annexation_of_Crimea_by_the_Russian_Federation" title="Annexation of Crimea by the Russian Federation">annexation</a> to the Russian Federation as the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Crimea" title="Republic of Crimea">Republic of Crimea</a>.
</p><p>In June 2016, in a <a href="/wiki/2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">referendum in the United Kingdom</a> on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Union%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="European Union–United Kingdom relations">country's membership in the European Union</a>, 52% of voters voted to leave the EU, leading to the complex <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a> separation process and negotiations, which led to <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_the_2016_United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum" title="Aftermath of the 2016 United Kingdom European Union membership referendum">political and economic changes</a> for both the UK and the remaining European Union countries. The UK left the EU on 31 January 2020. Later that year, Europe was affected by the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.
</p><p>
According to the <i>Wall Street Journal</i> in 2021 as <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> stepped down as the highly popular <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">Chancellor of Germany</a> after 16 years:</p><blockquote><p> Ms. Merkel leaves in her wake a weakened Europe, a region whose aspirations to act as a third <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpower</a> have come to seem ever more unrealistic. When she became chancellor in 2005, the EU was at a high point: It had adopted the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>, which was meant to rival the <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">dollar</a> as a <a href="/wiki/World_currency" title="World currency">global currency</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">had just expanded by absorbing former members of the Soviet bloc</a>. Today’s EU, by contrast, is geographically and economically diminished. Having lost the U.K. because of <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a>, it faces deep political and cultural divisions, lags behind in the global race for innovation and technology and is increasingly squeezed by the mounting <a href="/wiki/China%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="China–United States relations">U.S.-China strategic rivalry</a>. Europe has endured thanks in part to Ms. Merkel’s pragmatic stewardship, but it has been battered by crises during her entire time in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>Russia began an <a href="/wiki/2022_Russian_invasion_of_Ukraine" title="2022 Russian invasion of Ukraine">invasion of Ukraine</a> on 24 February 2022, in a major escalation of the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Ukrainian_War" title="Russo-Ukrainian War">Russo-Ukrainian War</a> that began in 2014. It is the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conventional_military_attack" title="Conventional military attack">conventional military attack</a> in Europe since World War II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[207]</a></sup>
</p><h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Chronology">Chronology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=History_of_Europe&amp;action=edit&amp;section=68" title="Edit section: Chronology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 30em;">* 7000 BC: <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> in Europe begins.
<ul><li>3850 BC: Malta's <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Temple_period&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Temple period (page does not exist)">Temple period</a> begins.</li>
<li>3500 BC: First European civilization, <a href="/wiki/Minoan_civilization" title="Minoan civilization">Minoan civilization</a>, begins on Crete.</li>
<li>3000 BC: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Europeans" title="Indo-Europeans">Indo-Europeans</a> begin a large-scale settlement of the continent.</li>
<li>2500 BC: <a href="/wiki/Stonehenge" title="Stonehenge">Stonehenge</a> is constructed.</li>
<li>2100 BC: First European script, <a href="/wiki/Cretan_hieroglyphs" title="Cretan hieroglyphs">Cretan hieroglyphs</a>, is invented by Minoans.</li>
<li>1750 BC: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mycenaean_civilization" title="Mycenaean civilization">Mycenaean civilization</a> begins.</li>
<li>1600 BC: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thera_eruption" title="Thera eruption">Thera eruption</a> occurs on the island of <a href="/wiki/Santorini" title="Santorini">Santorini</a>, destructing the Minoan city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thera" title="Thera">Thera</a>.</li>
<li>1450 BC: <a href="/wiki/Crete" title="Crete">Crete</a> is conquered by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mycenaeans" title="Mycenaeans">Mycenaeans</a>.</li>
<li>1200 BC: <a href="/wiki/Late_Bronze_Age_collapse" title="Late Bronze Age collapse">Late Bronze Age collapse</a> begins.</li>
<li>1100 BC: <a href="/wiki/Minoan_civilization" title="Minoan civilization">Minoan civilization</a> falls.</li>
<li>1050 BC: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mycenaean_civilization" title="Mycenaean civilization">Mycenaean civilization</a> falls after a period of palace destruction, marking the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Greek_Dark_Ages" title="Greek Dark Ages">Greek Dark Ages</a>.</li>
<li>900 BC: <a href="/wiki/Etruscan_civilization" title="Etruscan civilization">Etruscan civilization</a> begins.</li>
<li>800 BC: <a href="/wiki/Greek_Dark_Ages" title="Greek Dark Ages">Greek Dark Ages</a> end, marking the beginning of <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a>.</li>
<li>753 BC: Traditional year of founding of Rome.</li>
<li>700 BC: <a href="/wiki/Homer" title="Homer">Homer</a> composes <i><a href="/wiki/Iliad" title="Iliad">The Iliad</a></i>, an epic poem that represents the first extended work of European literature.</li>
<li>509 BC: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> is created.</li>
<li>499 BC: <a href="/wiki/Greco-Persian_Wars" title="Greco-Persian Wars">Greco-Persian Wars</a> begin.</li>
<li>449 BC: End of <a href="/wiki/Greco-Persian_Wars" title="Greco-Persian Wars">Greco-Persian Wars</a> with Greeks defeating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Achaemid_Empire" title="Achaemid Empire">Achaemid Empire</a>.</li>
<li>440 BC: <a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a> defends Athenian <a href="/wiki/Political_freedom" title="Political freedom">political freedom</a> in the <i><a href="/wiki/Histories_(Herodotus)" title="Histories (Herodotus)">Histories</a></i>.</li>
<li>323 BC: <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> dies and his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedonian_Empire" title="Macedonian Empire">Macedonian Empire</a> (reaching far into Asia) fragments.</li>
<li>264 BC: <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a> begin.</li>
<li>146 BC: <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a> end with destruction of <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthage</a>.</li>
<li>48 BC: <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>  crosses the Rubicon river, marking the beginning of a civil war.</li>
<li>44 BC: <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a> <a href="/wiki/Assassination_of_Julius_Caesar" title="Assassination of Julius Caesar">is murdered</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> enters its terminal crisis.</li>
<li>27 BC: Establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Octavian" title="Octavian">Octavian</a>.</li></ul>
<p><b>AD</b>
</p>
<ul><li>14 AD: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Octavian" title="Octavian">Octavian</a> dies.</li>
<li>30 or 33 AD: <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a>, a popular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Religious" title="Religious">religious</a> leader, is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crucifixion_of_Christ" title="Crucifixion of Christ">crucified</a>.</li>
<li>45–55 (ca): First <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> congregations in mainland Greece and in Rome.</li>
<li>68: First Roman imperial dynasty, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julio-Claudian" title="Julio-Claudian">Julio-Claudian</a>, ends with suicide of <a href="/wiki/Nero" title="Nero">Nero</a>.</li>
<li>79: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eruption_of_Vesuvius" title="Eruption of Vesuvius">Eruption of Vesuvius</a> occurs, buriing the cities of <a href="/wiki/Pompeii" title="Pompeii">Pompeii</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herculaneum" title="Herculaneum">Herculaneum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stabiae" title="Stabiae">Stabiae</a> under the ashes.</li>
<li>117: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a> reaches its territorial peak.</li>
<li>166: <a href="/wiki/Antonine_Plague" title="Antonine Plague">Antonine Plague</a> begins.</li>
<li>293: <a href="/wiki/Diocletian" title="Diocletian">Diocletian</a> reorganizes the Empire by creating the <a href="/wiki/Tetrarchy" title="Tetrarchy">Tetrarchy</a>.</li>
<li>313: <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine</a> officially recognises Christianity, marking the end of the persecution of Christians.</li>
<li>330: <a href="/wiki/Constantine_the_Great" title="Constantine the Great">Constantine</a> makes <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> into his capital, a <a href="/wiki/New_Rome" title="New Rome">new Rome</a>.</li>
<li>370: <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">Huns</a> first enter Europe.</li>
<li>395: Following the death of <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_I" title="Theodosius I">Theodosius I</a>, the Empire is permanently split into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" title="Eastern Roman Empire">Eastern Roman Empire</a> (later Byzantium) and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>.</li>
<li>476: <a href="/wiki/Odoacer" title="Odoacer">Odoacer</a> captures <a href="/wiki/Ravenna" title="Ravenna">Ravenna</a> and deposes the last Roman emperor in the west: traditionally seen as the end date of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>.</li>
<li>527: <a href="/wiki/Justinian_I" title="Justinian I">Justinian I</a> is <a href="/wiki/Coronation" title="Coronation">crowned</a> emperor of <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantium</a>. Orders the editing of <i><a href="/wiki/Corpus_Juris_Civilis" title="Corpus Juris Civilis">Corpus Juris Civilis</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Digest_(Roman_law)" title="Digest (Roman law)">Digest (Roman law)</a>.</li>
<li>597: Beginning of Roman Catholic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christianization_of_Anglo-Saxon_England" title="Christianization of Anglo-Saxon England">Christianization of Anglo-Saxon England</a> (missions and churches had been in existence well before this date, but their contacts with Rome had been loose or nonexistent)</li>
<li>600: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Columbanus" title="Saint Columbanus">Saint Columbanus</a> uses the term "Europe" in a letter.</li>
<li>655: <a href="/wiki/Jus_patronatus" title="Jus patronatus">Jus patronatus</a>.</li>
<li>681: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khan_Asparukh" title="Khan Asparukh">Khan Asparukh</a> leads the <a href="/wiki/Bulgars" title="Bulgars">Bulgars</a> and in a union with the numerous <a href="/wiki/Seven_Slavic_tribes" title="Seven Slavic tribes">local</a> <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">Slavs</a> invades the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine_empire" title="Byzantine empire">Byzantine empire</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ongal" title="Battle of Ongal">Battle of Ongal</a>, creating <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">Bulgaria</a>.</li>
<li>718: <a href="/wiki/Tervel_of_Bulgaria" title="Tervel of Bulgaria">Tervel of Bulgaria</a> helps the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> stop the Arabic invasion of Europe, and breaks the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Constantinople_(717%E2%80%93718)" title="Siege of Constantinople (717–718)">siege of Constantinople</a>.</li>
<li>722: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Covadonga" title="Battle of Covadonga">Battle of Covadonga</a> in the Iberian Peninsula. <a href="/wiki/Pelagius_of_Asturias" title="Pelagius of Asturias">Pelayo</a>, a noble Visigoth, defeats a Muslim army that tried to conquer the Cantabrian coast. This helps establish the Christian <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Asturias" title="Kingdom of Asturias">Kingdom of Asturias</a>, and marks the beginning of the Reconquista.</li>
<li>732: At the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tours" title="Battle of Tours">Battle of Tours</a>, the Franks stop the advance of the Arabs into Europe.</li>
<li>800: Coronation of <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> as <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>.</li>
<li>813: Third Council of Tours: Priests are ordered to preach in the <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">native language of the population</a>.</li>
<li>843: <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Verdun" title="Treaty of Verdun">Treaty of Verdun</a>.</li>
<li>863: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saints_Cyril_and_Methodius" title="Saints Cyril and Methodius">Saints Cyril and Methodius</a> arrive in <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">Great Moravia</a>, initiating Christian mission among the Slav peoples.</li>
<li>864: <a href="/wiki/Boris_I_of_Bulgaria" title="Boris I of Bulgaria">Boris I of Bulgaria</a> <a href="/wiki/Christianization_of_Bulgaria" title="Christianization of Bulgaria">officially baptises the whole nation</a>, converting the non-Christian population from <a href="/wiki/Tengrism" title="Tengrism">Tengrism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slavic_paganism" title="Slavic paganism">Slavic</a> and other paganism to <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, and officially founding the <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Orthodox_Church" title="Bulgarian Orthodox Church">Bulgarian Church</a></li>
<li>872: <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Norway" title="Unification of Norway">Unification of Norway</a>.</li>
<li>886: <a href="/wiki/Bulgarians" title="Bulgarians">Bulgarian</a> students of <a href="/wiki/Cyril_and_Methodius" title="Cyril and Methodius">Cyril and Methodius</a> – Sava, <a href="/wiki/Clement_of_Ohrid" title="Clement of Ohrid">Kliment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Naum" title="Saint Naum">Naum</a>, Gorazd, Angelariy – arrive back to <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Empire" title="Bulgarian Empire">Bulgaria</a>, creating the <a href="/wiki/Preslav_Literary_School" title="Preslav Literary School">Preslav</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ohrid_Literary_School" title="Ohrid Literary School">Ohrid</a> Literary Schools.</li>
<li>893: The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyrillic_alphabet" title="Cyrillic alphabet">Cyrillic alphabet</a>, developed during the 9th century AD at the <a href="/wiki/Preslav_Literary_School" title="Preslav Literary School">Preslav Literary School</a> in the <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">First Bulgarian Empire</a>, becomes the official <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_alphabet" title="Bulgarian alphabet">Bulgarian alphabet</a>.</li>
<li>895: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" title="Hungarian people">Hungarian people</a> led by <a href="/wiki/%C3%81rp%C3%A1d" title="Árpád">Árpád</a> start to settle in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carpathian_Basin" title="Carpathian Basin">Carpathian Basin</a>.</li>
<li>917: In the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Achelous_(917)" title="Battle of Achelous (917)">Battle of Achelous (917)</a> <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> defeats the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine_empire" title="Byzantine empire">Byzantine empire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Simeon_I_of_Bulgaria" title="Simeon I of Bulgaria">Simeon I of Bulgaria</a> is proclaimed as emperor, thus <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> becomes an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bulgarian_empire" title="Bulgarian empire">empire</a>.</li>
<li>962: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otto_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Otto I, Holy Roman Emperor">Otto I</a> of <a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">East Francia</a> is crowned as "Emperor" by the Pope, beginning the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>.</li>
<li>988 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kievan_Rus" title="Kievan Rus">Kievan Rus</a> adopts Christianity, often seen as the origin of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodox Church</a>.</li>
<li>1054: Start of the <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">East–West Schism</a>, which divides the Christian church for centuries.</li>
<li>1066: Successful <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_England" title="Norman conquest of England">Norman Invasion</a> of England by <a href="/wiki/William_the_Conqueror" title="William the Conqueror">William the Conqueror</a>.</li>
<li>1095: <a href="/wiki/Pope_Urban_II" title="Pope Urban II">Pope Urban II</a> calls for the <a href="/wiki/First_Crusade" title="First Crusade">First Crusade</a>.</li>
<li>12th century: The <a href="/wiki/12th_century_in_literature" title="12th century in literature">12th century in literature</a> saw an increase in the number of texts. The <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_of_the_12th_century" title="Renaissance of the 12th century">Renaissance of the 12th century</a> occurs.</li>
<li>1128: <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_S%C3%A3o_Mamede" title="Battle of São Mamede">Battle of São Mamede</a>, formation of Portuguese sovereignty.</li>
<li>1131: Birth of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sicily" title="Kingdom of Sicily">Kingdom of Sicily</a></li>
<li>1185: <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_Empire" title="Bulgarian Empire">Bulgarian</a> sovereignty was reestablished with the <a href="/wiki/Uprising_of_Asen_and_Peter" title="Uprising of Asen and Peter">anti-Byzantine uprising of the Bulgarians and Vlachs</a></li>
<li>1250: Death of <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick II, Holy Roman Emperor">emperor Frederick II</a>; end of effective ability of emperors to exercise control in Italy.</li>
<li>1303: The period of the <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">Crusades</a> is over.</li>
<li>1309–1378: The <a href="/wiki/Avignon_Papacy" title="Avignon Papacy">Avignon Papacy</a></li>
<li>1315–1317: The <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_of_1315%E2%80%931317" title="Great Famine of 1315–1317">Great Famine of 1315–1317</a> in Northern Europe</li>
<li>1341: <a href="/wiki/Petrarch" title="Petrarch">Petrarch</a>, the "Father of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renaissance_Humanism" title="Renaissance Humanism">Humanism</a>", becomes the first <a href="/wiki/Poet_laureate" title="Poet laureate">poet laureate</a> since antiquity.</li>
<li>1337–1453: The <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years' War">Hundred Years' War</a> between England and France.</li>
<li>1348–1351: <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> kills about one-third of Europe's population.</li>
<li>1439: <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Gutenberg" title="Johannes Gutenberg">Johannes Gutenberg</a> invents first <a href="/wiki/Movable_type" title="Movable type">movable type</a> and the first <a href="/wiki/Printing_press" title="Printing press">printing press</a> for books, starting the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Printing_Revolution" title="Printing Revolution">Printing Revolution</a>.</li>
<li>1453: <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">Fall of Constantinople</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turks" title="Ottoman Turks">Ottoman Turks</a>.</li>
<li>1487: The <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_the_Roses" title="Wars of the Roses">Wars of the Roses</a> end.</li>
<li>1492: The <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a> ends in the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>. A Spanish expeditionary group, commanded by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>, lands in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>.</li>
<li>1497: <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a> departs to India starting direct trade with Asia.</li>
<li>1498: <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> paints <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Last_Supper_(Leonardo_da_Vinci)" title="The Last Supper (Leonardo da Vinci)">The Last Supper</a></i> in Milan as the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> flourishes.</li>
<li>1508: <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor">Maximilian I</a> the last ruling "<a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Romans" title="King of the Romans">King of the Romans</a>" and the first "elected Emperor of the Romans".</li>
<li>1517: <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> nails his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/95_theses" title="95 theses">95 theses</a> on indulgences to the door of the <a href="/wiki/All_Saints%27_Church,_Wittenberg" title="All Saints' Church, Wittenberg">church</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wittenberg" title="Wittenberg">Wittenberg</a>, triggering discussions which would soon lead to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Reformation</a></li>
<li>1519: <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Ferdinand Magellan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Juan_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Elcano" title="Juan Sebastián Elcano">Juan Sebastián Elcano</a> begin first global circumnavigation. Their expedition returns in 1522.</li>
<li>1519: <a href="/wiki/Hern%C3%A1n_Cort%C3%A9s" title="Hernán Cortés">Hernán Cortés</a> begins conquest of Mexico for Spain.</li>
<li>1532: <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Pizarro" title="Francisco Pizarro">Francisco Pizarro</a> begins the conquest of Peru (the <a href="/wiki/Inca_Empire" title="Inca Empire">Inca Empire</a>) for Spain.</li>
<li>1543: <a href="/wiki/Nicolaus_Copernicus" title="Nicolaus Copernicus">Nicolaus Copernicus</a> publishes <i><a href="/wiki/De_revolutionibus_orbium_coelestium" title="De revolutionibus orbium coelestium">De revolutionibus orbium coelestium</a> (On the Revolutions of the Celestial Spheres)</i>.</li>
<li>1547: The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Grand Duchy of Moscow</a> becomes the <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsardom of Russia</a>.</li>
<li>1582: The introduction of the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">Gregorian calendar</a>; Russia refuses to adopt it until 1918.</li>
<li>1610: <a href="/wiki/Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei">Galileo Galilei</a> uses his telescope to discover the moons of <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">Jupiter</a>.</li>
<li>1618: The <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">Thirty Years' War</a> brings massive devastation to central Europe.</li>
<li>1648: The <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" title="Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a> ends the Thirty Years' War, and introduces the principle of the integrity of the nation state.</li>
<li>1687: <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a> publishes <i><a href="/wiki/Philosophi%C3%A6_Naturalis_Principia_Mathematica" title="Philosophiæ Naturalis Principia Mathematica">Principia Mathematica</a></i>, having a profound impact on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Enlightenment" title="The Enlightenment">The Enlightenment</a>.</li>
<li>1699: <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Karlowitz" title="Treaty of Karlowitz">Treaty of Karlowitz</a> concludes the <a href="/wiki/Great_Turkish_War" title="Great Turkish War">Austro-Ottoman War</a>. This marks the end of Ottoman control of Central Europe and the beginning of Ottoman stagnation, establishing the Habsburg monarchy as the dominant power in Central and Southeastern Europe.</li>
<li>1700: Outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">Great Northern War</a>. The first would check the aspirations of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV" title="Louis XIV">Louis XIV</a>, king of France to dominate European affairs; the second would lead to Russia's emergence as a great power and a recognizably European state.</li>
<li>18th century: <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Age of Enlightenment</a> spurs an intellectual renaissance across Europe.</li>
<li>1707: The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Kingdom of Great Britain</a> is formed by the union of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a>.</li>
<li>1712: <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Newcomen" title="Thomas Newcomen">Thomas Newcomen</a> invents first practical steam engine which begins <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> in Britain.</li>
<li>1721: Foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>.</li>
<li>1775: <a href="/wiki/James_Watt" title="James Watt">James Watt</a> invents a new efficient steam engine accelerating the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> in Britain.</li>
<li>1776: <a href="/wiki/Adam_Smith" title="Adam Smith">Adam Smith</a> publishes <a href="/wiki/The_Wealth_of_Nations" title="The Wealth of Nations">The Wealth of Nations</a>.</li>
<li>1784: <a href="/wiki/Immanuel_Kant" title="Immanuel Kant">Immanuel Kant</a> publishes <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Answering_the_Question:_What_Is_Enlightenment%3F" title="Answering the Question: What Is Enlightenment?">Answering the Question: What Is Enlightenment?</a></i>.</li>
<li>1789: Beginning of the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> and end of the absolute monarchy in France.</li>
<li>1792–1802: <a href="/wiki/French_Revolutionary_Wars" title="French Revolutionary Wars">French Revolutionary Wars</a>.</li>
<li>1799: <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> <a href="/wiki/Coup_of_18_Brumaire" title="Coup of 18 Brumaire">comes to power</a>, eventually consolidating his position as <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_the_French" title="Emperor of the French">Emperor of the French</a>.</li>
<li>1803–1815: <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a> end in defeat of Napoleon.</li>
<li>1806: Napoleon abolishes the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>.</li>
<li>1814–1815: <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>; Treaty of Vienna; France is reduced to 1789 boundaries; Reactionary forces dominate across Europe.</li>
<li>1825: <a href="/wiki/George_Stephenson" title="George Stephenson">George Stephenson</a> opens the <a href="/wiki/Stockton_and_Darlington_Railway" title="Stockton and Darlington Railway">Stockton and Darlington Railway</a> the first steam train railway for passenger traffic in the world.</li>
<li>1830: The southern provinces secede from the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="United Kingdom of the Netherlands">United Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Revolution" title="Belgian Revolution">Belgian Revolution</a>.</li>
<li>1836: <a href="/wiki/Louis_Daguerre" title="Louis Daguerre">Louis Daguerre</a> invents first practical photographic method, in effect the first camera.</li>
<li>1838: <a href="/wiki/SS_Great_Western" title="SS Great Western">SS <i>Great Western</i></a>, the first steamship built for regularly scheduled transatlantic crossings enters service.</li>
